Here is a photo of the attendant defying the face covering mandate on Tuesday July 7th at approximately 1615 hours.

‚ÄúBecause of our collective actions, California has limited the spread of COVID-19 and associated hospitalizations and deaths in our state. Still, the risk for COVID-19 remains and the increasing number of Californians who are leaving their homes for work and other needs, increases the risk for COVID-19 exposure and infection.
Over the last four months, we have learned a lot about COVID-19 transmission, most notably that people who are infected but are asymptomatic or pre- symptomatic play an important part in community spread. The use of face coverings by everyone can limit the release of infected droplets when talking, coughing, and/or sneezing, as well as reinforce physical distancing.
This document updates existing CDPH guidance for the use of cloth face coverings by the general public when outside the home. It mandates that face coverings be worn state-wide in the circumstances and with the exceptions outlined below. It does not substitute for existing guidance about social distancing and handwashing.
Guidance
People in California must wear face coverings when they are in the high-risk situations listed below:
‚Ä¢ Inside of, or in line to enter, any indoor public space;1
‚Ä¢ Obtaining services from the healthcare sector in settings including, but not limited to, a hospital, pharmacy, medical clinic, laboratory, physician or dental office, veterinary clinic, or blood bank;2
‚Ä¢ Waiting for or riding on public transportation or paratransit or while in a taxi, private car service, or ride-sharing vehicle;
‚Ä¢ Engaged in work, whether at the workplace or performing work off-site, when:
‚Ä¢ Interacting in-person with any member of the public;
‚Ä¢ Working in any space visited by members of the public, regardless of whether anyone from the public is present at the time;‚Äù</Text>

3. I wouldn't bother cleaning or painting the place after moving out since you will be charged regardless.

< text>
I have lived at Altitude for about 6 months and am super happy with the apartment! First off shout out to Shaunessey, Adriana, Eli and Erik for your kindness and always helping out with whatever we need! They are the friendliest staff!

In short Altitude is perfect if you looking for something new/updated/comfortable in West LA that isn't an outdated 1950s rental unit or a gross, dingy apartment.

My husband, dog and I share a 1BR/BA apartment and we have been very comfortable in our space. As far as our apartment goes we are very happy with the unit, appliances, A/C, etc. and we haven't had any problems. If you need a repair the maintenance staff takes care of it within 24 hours.

As far as the amenities go the pool, gym and other public area are very comfortable and we haven't had an issue with anything being overcrowded. The neighborhood is very safe during day and night, which is especially nice as we are dog owners and are in and out a lot. (Also for dog owners they have a pet washing area.) Since the area is mostly corporate offices it is generally fairly quiet during nights and weekends, even with busy HH down the road.

The HH Center, though under renovation, is in walking distance with several casual dining options.< /text>

<Text>We have passed Izakaya Wasa probably 100 times in Irvine Spectrum.
For some reason, we've never tried the place.
We finally stepped in for the first.
And we were quite happy with our dinner experience.

We ordered two entrees to share.
The first one was Poke Don.
Large pieces of fresh sashimi included salmon, tuna, albacore, yellowtail, halibut, and shrimp.
The poke sauce was traditional style with sesame oil.
We prefer the Japanese style poke more than the American style with mayonnaise sauce.
The poke bowl was very good, and portion was huge.
It also came with a bowl of miso soup.

The second entree was the 3 items combination dinner.
There were so many good choices for the items, and it was hard to decide what items to order.
We opted for teriyaki beef, sesame chicken, and spicy tuna rolls.
When the bento box came to the table, we were very surprised by how large the portion was.
Included with the 3 items were miso soup, rice, salad, seaweed salad, and shumai.
We were expecting 2 pieces of spicy tuna rolls with the combination.
Instead we got 8 pieces, a whole roll!
Teriyaki beef was cooked to medium. Very tender.
The teriyaki sauce was not overly sweet, just the way we like it.
Sesame chicken was not bad, but it wasn't what we expected.
We thought it was the fried chicken pieces without any sauce.
Izakaya Wasa's version had a sweet and spicy sauce over the fried chicken.
Love the seaweed salad and Japanese shumai.

Ôº∑e are glad that now we have another great choice for food in Irvine Spectrum.
Will definitely return again to try more food on the menu.< /Text>< rating>

<Rating>5<//Rating><Response>None</Response><Pictures>None</Pictures><Date>1486671506367< /Date><Name>Sean Schluntz</Name><userid>102075195216525523515< /userid>< Review>
The San Francisco Bay Area is blessed with many great theaters and this is one of the more accessible gems. There is a parking lot attached (get there early though as it fills up quickly) and it's an easy 1/5 mile walk from the Walnut Creek BART station. It's also surrounded by a wide variety of food options.

The theater seats a good number of people, but it's not so big that you any of the seats would really be considered bad. The box seats in the balcony are great for spoken work and bands (though you might want to bring earplugs because the speakers are hanging right next to you) but I don't recommend them for theatrical performances as you'll miss some of what is on your side and be looking into the wings of the stage from the opposite side. The acoustics are good throughout (though like I said it can get quite loud in the balcony boxes).

The lobby and floors have a good amount of space so hanging out with friends isn't too crowded while you are waiting for the house to open.< /Review>

<review>You were PROMPT; you kept me INFORMED of all developments of the upcoming job at hand; you performed the job RAPIDLY; you performed the job EFFICIENTLY; and, you performed the job, with COMPASSION. I also imagine that you, in addition, would have viable alternatives at your fingertips, for any item(s), that you cannot remove. THANKS A MILLION!!

There has some "beefing" about G.J's. charging any Fee at all. Well, the reason G.J. became a solution for me, is that I believe that operational costs for the old-line charitable organizations, has become prohibitive, for door-to-door rummage pickups, so much so, that they're phasing those out, in favor of Automobile Donations. And they're sometimes backed up months in advance, too--not terribly convenient.

So now, you often have to schlep your rummage yourself, down to the Thrift Store/Processing Center--and schlep stuff right back home, if they don't want it.

If, more and more folks use G.J., perhaps you may then see a reduction in the rates that they charge.</review>< Gmap_id>
